  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fc504bd6-1340-43f8-9b62-1404746428c3'

    }

  <span id="freeText8548910761399549158" style="display:none">“I’m the class nerd, the only kid who doesn’t get invited to birthday parties… Maybe it would be better if everyone gave me the silent treatment. Ever since, Andy can see all kinds of ghosts and talk to them, and that's why he is the only one who can save the lovely Zoe from the evil spirit that got into her home. <span id="freeTextContainer17826928138554004331">I bought this book to read to the kids I read to in grammar schools around L.A. I started reading it and I found I couldn't put it down. It's the kind of book that is about discovering your strength, overcoming bullies, and first love. It's also about finding your confidence and belief in yourself. The story revolves around Andy who is the class nerd and is picked on a lot. His best friend is his Grandfather. Not giving anything away, his Grandfather helps Andy with love and self belief in a spi</span>
  <span id="freeText17826928138554004331" style="display:none">I bought this book to read to the kids I read to in grammar schools around L.A. I started reading it and I found I couldn't put it down. It's the kind of book that is about discovering your strength, overcoming bullies, and first love. It's also about finding your confidence and belief in yourself. The story revolves around Andy who is the class nerd and is picked on a lot. His best friend is his Grandfather. Not giving anything away, his Grandfather helps Andy with love and self belief in a spiritual way. I really connected with the way this came to happen. I even cried because of the situation. <br />This is going to be a great book for me to read to kids. The chapters are short so I can do short or long readings and the story is so compelling it makes you want to continue reading. I hope this character continues in other books because I will definitely buy them. </span>

  <span id="freeText15699600997229319970" style="display:none">I thought that this was a fantastic children's read, dealing gently with the subject of death.<br /><br />Andy is the class nerd. No-one likes him and no-one talks to him. Even his parents and sister don't want much to do with him. He's smarter than most and the only person in his life who understands him is Grandpa. When he finds out that Grandpa has terminal cancer and just a few days to live, the bottom drops out of his world. The good news is that Grandpa has not gone forever and returns to help Andy in the form a ghostly spirit. Grandpa's mission: to help Andy get the love of his life to the movies!<br /><br />Will Andy ever be able to summon enough courage to speak to the lovely Zoe? Will he save her house from burning down? Can he convince his parents and his therapist that he's not crazy? You'll just have to read on to find out more!<br /><br />This was a fantastic 5 star read, which will appeal to both children and adults alike.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer852842475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17139761718098652237">This is a very heart filled book. It is a story about a boy that doesn’t fit in at school or home. I read the whole book in one sitting. After every chapter, I kept wanting to know more until I had read the whole book! I really enjoyed the illustrations also. They give you a good visual experience about the characters in the story and what is going on.<br/><br/>This book is very detailed and well written! It falls into several categories, Romance-for the love of his life. This book teaches you to never st</span>
  <span id="freeText17139761718098652237" style="display:none">This is a very heart filled book. It is a story about a boy that doesn’t fit in at school or home. I read the whole book in one sitting. After every chapter, I kept wanting to know more until I had read the whole book! I really enjoyed the illustrations also. They give you a good visual experience about the characters in the story and what is going on.<br /><br />This book is very detailed and well written! It falls into several categories, Romance-for the love of his life. This book teaches you to never stop trying to win the person you love. It teaches you to believe in yourself. Bullying- is a big issue right now. This book should be promoted with the books about bullying. Loss of a person you love. This book brought tears to my eyes as I connected with the writer. I also lost my grandpa to cancer. My grandmother shortly followed him with Alzheimer’s. It also teaches children to wear helmets when they ride their bicycles. Then the book turns into a sweet and spooky ghost story, which explains how the character became a superhero. I loved how the ending tied in with the beginning. I love how it has a happy ending and doesn’t leaving you wondering about anything.<br /><br />I won’t say anymore, or I will give the entire book away! I honestly really enjoyed this book and highly recommend it to everyone. There are a lot of lessons to be learned in this book that makes it very educational also. This book definitely deserves a 5 star rating!!!<br /></span>

I love how the author included illustrations for each chapter to kind of give the reader a feel of what's happening in the author's eyes as well as the reader's. A very cool book that I would recommend to any young reader (my 7 year old enjoyed it, though I read it to her).<br /><br />Reviewed by IABookReviews.com</span>

  <span id="freeText18121096044305024661" style="display:none">This is a great little book for the middle grades set. It’s a heartwarming tale of the class nerd/geek who is in love with the prettiest girl in the class. When a family tragedy strikes, the main character (Andy) develops some supernatural powers that change him from geek to hero. It’s written with a lot of heart and both the storyline and characters are well-developed. I loved it and wish I’d find more books like this for my kids to enjoy. Really hoping to read more from this author and share his wonderful world with my young ones. Well done and highly recommended.</span>

<div id="review_815617920" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/815617920" />
    <a title="Lokiie1984" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26670009-lokiie1984"><img alt="Lokiie1984" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/815617920?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lokiie1984" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lokiie1984" href="/user/show/26670009-lokiie1984">Lokiie1984</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer815617920" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8920933823191853941">Whether you’re an adult with children or a child yourself or just someone reminiscing about when you were in grade school, Andy is very easy to relate to. I mean who didn't feel like an outcast in school. Especially when you were different then everyone else or if you weren't good with sports. And how many of would have loved to have some special ability that us see "grandpa" who was only there to help us get through those hard times. <br/><br/>This is one of those books that belongs in a grade school cla</span>
  <span id="freeText8920933823191853941" style="display:none">Whether you’re an adult with children or a child yourself or just someone reminiscing about when you were in grade school, Andy is very easy to relate to. I mean who didn't feel like an outcast in school. Especially when you were different then everyone else or if you weren't good with sports. And how many of would have loved to have some special ability that us see "grandpa" who was only there to help us get through those hard times. <br /><br />This is one of those books that belongs in a grade school class library. Personally, I would have loved it as a kid. <br /><br />So as always I try to talk about the things I liked about the story and the things I didn’t like. <br /><br />Positive: Overall, I enjoyed everything about the book. But if I had to pick a few things that stood out more than the others, I think it would be the artwork. While its simple in its design it did the job very well and as I read I wanted to figure out how each drawing related to the chapter. Otherwise like I said above, the story is very well done.<br /><br />Negative: One thing that I didn’t care for was the point of view, however that said Gadot does it in a way that makes it feel like we are reading Andy's journal or diary so the POV makes perfect sense. Another minor thing I saw was that he some pretty long paragraphs that I feel could have been broken up to make the reading a little easier, but by no means did they hurt the story in anyway. <br /><br />And finally a personal preference *Spoiler warning* While the goal of the story is for Andy to become confident enough to ask Zoe out on a date, I would have rather him ended up with Sally as she was more like him. A nerd girl for a nerd guy. But in the end, we find out that maybe Zoe is a little more like Andy then we ever thought. So maybe in book number two we will find out that it’s more like a Boy that sees ghosts dating a girl that sees ghosts. In that case, I think it works out just fine.<br /><br />Again, I would highly recommend the book to anyone with kids or just kids in general. And I personally am looking forward to number two.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8920933823191853941" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_825596824" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/825596824" />
    <a title="Molly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25345234-molly"><img alt="Molly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383699067p2/25345234.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/825596824?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Molly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Molly" href="/user/show/25345234-molly">Molly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer825596824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3263800095694333932">Fun, educational and sweet<br/><br/>I got this book for my nephew but I wanted to read it first, just to make sure it wouldn’t be too mature for him (you never know). I was surprised that I enjoyed the book so much!<br/><br/>I love that it is told from Andy’s perspective, the author really nailed how it feels to be a love-sick awkward boy that just yearns to be understood. He wants so badly to fit in but he soon learns that being yourself and being unique is the key to not only acceptance by his peers but also true</span>
  <span id="freeText3263800095694333932" style="display:none">Fun, educational and sweet<br /><br />I got this book for my nephew but I wanted to read it first, just to make sure it wouldn’t be too mature for him (you never know). I was surprised that I enjoyed the book so much!<br /><br />I love that it is told from Andy’s perspective, the author really nailed how it feels to be a love-sick awkward boy that just yearns to be understood. He wants so badly to fit in but he soon learns that being yourself and being unique is the key to not only acceptance by his peers but also true happiness. This is such an important lesson that many adults have yet to figure out. Accept yourself first before others can.<br /><br />The tragedy of losing the one person he can really confide in and who fully supports him was so hard to read but it was handled very well. Then add in the supernatural superpowers allowing Andy to speak with his grandpa again and you have an awesome story! It was so heartwarming and helped with his grief. Then in a neat twist to the plot, the girl he is in love with is in danger by an evil spirit and Andy has the ability to intervene and save her and her family. He goes from being the reserved bullied nerd to the hero, how better to get the girl’s attention?<br /><br />I really enjoyed this book and my nephew is currently reading it and so far he is just as glued to the pages as I was! Would definitely recommend this book to boys and girls alike, especially those that feel like outcasts or are uncomfortable in their own skin. Finding yourself is a journey and the sooner you learn the important lessons taught in this book the faster you can reach happiness.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3263800095694333932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_906391505" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/906391505" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5765641-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395238899p2/5765641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/906391505?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/5765641-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Kids and parents</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Christine by: </span>
      Myself
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer906391505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6891017591644311106">I think I may be one of the few adults who purchased this book without the intention to read it to a child. The Kindle look inside feature told me I was going to love it because I fell for Andy in the very first paragraph. I honestly can’t remember connecting immediately with a character like that before, so kudos to the author for rendering me spellbound so quickly. <br/><br/>Andy is insecure, put upon, virtually friendless and bullied. The prose is simple, but I found it evocative and intelligent. It ma</span>
  <span id="freeText6891017591644311106" style="display:none">I think I may be one of the few adults who purchased this book without the intention to read it to a child. The Kindle look inside feature told me I was going to love it because I fell for Andy in the very first paragraph. I honestly can’t remember connecting immediately with a character like that before, so kudos to the author for rendering me spellbound so quickly. <br /><br />Andy is insecure, put upon, virtually friendless and bullied. The prose is simple, but I found it evocative and intelligent. It made me think of all the kids out there, under similar circumstances, who lash out in horrendous ways and are driven to violence by those dark thoughts. Andy’s character could’ve been taken in any direction, but seemingly the love and attention from his Grandpa gives him what he needs to keep him on the straight and narrow. This book might encourage parents of the pre-teen set to begin a dialogue with their kids, see what's not being said and take the opportunity to slow down, and give some one-on-one.<br /><br />The paranormal elements were wonderful. Kids who really enjoy the Goosebumps series will love Supernatural Hero. Anyone who read Blume's Tales of a Fourth Grade Nothing will love this, too. It's entertaining, but delivers a message. For kids, it's that no matter how hard things seem now, they've got it in them to overcome anything that stands in their way. Nerds can be heroes. For adults, the message is they should find a way to connect and listen to their kids, talk without talking down to them.<br /><br />The afterward spoke of the author's children and family and told of the inspiration they provide. It touched my heart. And I have to mention the illustrations at the beginning of each chapter were amazing, so now I've got my eye on the paperback version. A perfect book all the way around.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6891017591644311106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_830944141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/830944141" />
    <a title="Kt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13085681-kt"><img alt="Kt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384294924p2/13085681.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/830944141?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kt" href="/user/show/13085681-kt">Kt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13085681-kt?shelf=kid-recs">kid-recs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer830944141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2113176011821204060">This was a really enjoyable story. Andy is a socially isolated middle school age boy. He is a sweet good hearted person that is often misunderstood. This book deals with many important themes. The illness and death of a loved one is center stage. The story also covers dealing with bullying at school, dealing with a difficult sibling, and living up to expectations of your parents. <br/><br/>Andy is lonely; he has only one friend near his age and a serious crush on one of the most popular girls in his class</span>
  <span id="freeText2113176011821204060" style="display:none">This was a really enjoyable story. Andy is a socially isolated middle school age boy. He is a sweet good hearted person that is often misunderstood. This book deals with many important themes. The illness and death of a loved one is center stage. The story also covers dealing with bullying at school, dealing with a difficult sibling, and living up to expectations of your parents. <br /><br />Andy is lonely; he has only one friend near his age and a serious crush on one of the most popular girls in his class. He never gets invited to parties and had a lot of anxiety about interacting with others. His grandpa is the one person that Andy feels understands him completely. The supernatural elements to this story are well done but not too scary for the younger set. <br /><br />I like the characters,they are authentic and relatable. Andy learns a lot during this story, and we get to cheer him on. This is more than a fantasy story; it is a growing up story. Andy learns to deal with life and its twists and sadness. I really enjoyed this book. It was heartwarming and funny. I plan to recommend it to my nephews and nieces. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2113176011821204060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13509358094837239897">Simply Enchanting! A Magical Journey that is Both Heartwarming & Inspirational!<br/><br/>A delightfully enchanting journey that will Capture your imagination and steal your heart! My daughter loves this story! We are reading it for the second time now. It is a wonderful story that not only focuses on valuable lessons but, also encourages children to aspire to be everything they dream of being.   <span id="freeText13509358094837239897" style="display:none">Simply Enchanting! A Magical Journey that is Both Heartwarming &amp; Inspirational!<br /><br />A delightfully enchanting journey that will Capture your imagination and steal your heart! My daughter loves this story! We are reading it for the second time now. It is a wonderful story that not only focuses on valuable lessons but, also encourages children to aspire to be everything they dream of being. Very Inspiring and perfect for middle school age children! She could really identify with Andy, the main character and his struggles with being different and feeling like an outsider. The author did a fabulous job of bringing the characters to life with depth and emotion that enables readers to really connect with them. As you witness Andy growing through some painful times you find yourself cheering him on as if he was your closest friend.<br /><br />Andy may be bullied at school, ignored at home when not being bullied by his older sister but, most of the time he just feels invisible. He soon learns just how very unique and special he really is. We witness Andy losing his best friend, his grandfather and your heart breaks for him , his struggle with understanding and his grief…Soon we are rejoicing with him as he moves through this tragedy and realizes he has very special powers and abilities. We root for Andy to get the girl he has loved for so very long, Zoe. <br /><br />Written from Andy’s point of view it truly keeps the reader’s attention and captures some of life’s most valuable lessons as we watch him grow through many of life’s common struggles with growing up. The author touches on the grief and pain of losing a loved one, remembering times past, self-confidence and insecurity and young love. With each challenge he moves through we watch him strengthen his own sense of self. A memorable story that will capture your heart! I highly recommend it to all parents for their kids to read. It brings to light feelings and situations that everyone will connect with on some level. Fantastic Job!<br /></span>

<div id="review_906004246" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/906004246" />
    <a title="Rae Ryans" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7223175-rae-ryans"><img alt="Rae Ryans" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442653104p2/7223175.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/906004246?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rae Ryans" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rae Ryans" href="/user/show/7223175-rae-ryans">Rae Ryans</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer906004246" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3773338219305122913">I originally picked up Supernatural Hero for my eleven year old son, but wow, was I impressed! Like most parents I read the book before giving it over to him so check for topics I don't want him reading, or that he won't understand. I loved it, and I'm not just saying I loved it for my son, I'm a true fan of Eran Gadot now!<br/><br/>The character development and story line is amazing for a book in this age range. Gadot really takes most of us back to our middle school days. Insecurities, annoying siblings</span>
  <span id="freeText3773338219305122913" style="display:none">I originally picked up Supernatural Hero for my eleven year old son, but wow, was I impressed! Like most parents I read the book before giving it over to him so check for topics I don't want him reading, or that he won't understand. I loved it, and I'm not just saying I loved it for my son, I'm a true fan of Eran Gadot now!<br /><br />The character development and story line is amazing for a book in this age range. Gadot really takes most of us back to our middle school days. Insecurities, annoying siblings, parents that don't get us, and tragically losing a beloved grandparent.<br /><br />The most wonderful part of this story is the way the author weaved so many different types of child into one character anyone can connect with. I think boys and girls will relate just fine with Andy our "hero" nerd.<br /><br />It does have supernatural elements that deal with Andy seeing and interacting with ghosts. It is all lighthearted and nothing scary or overly mature, so it won't upset sensitive children. I think the most powerful element of the story is believing in yourself, setting goals, and working hard to get them. The love story aspect isn't so overwhelming that young boys will shy away, but strong enough that girls will relate.<br /><br />I really hope Eran Gadot makes this into a series, it has all the makings for a great one. I recommend this for Kids in the 10+, and any adults or parents looking for a touching, fun throwback to their childhood.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3773338219305122913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2892008-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291075269p2/2892008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/955310277?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/2892008-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer955310277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5951712300510606745">This is a fantastic and entertaining book for middle grade kids! Written in a casual style from 11-year-old Andy’s point of view, the book captures young readers from the very beginning. <br/><br/>Andy is a “nerd” with few friends and has trouble connecting with his family and other kids his own age. His only real friend is his grandpa, who seems to be the only one who understands Andy and his strange ability to speak to those who have already died, like his grandma. But once his grandpa passes away rathe</span>
  <span id="freeText5951712300510606745" style="display:none">This is a fantastic and entertaining book for middle grade kids! Written in a casual style from 11-year-old Andy’s point of view, the book captures young readers from the very beginning. <br /><br />Andy is a “nerd” with few friends and has trouble connecting with his family and other kids his own age. His only real friend is his grandpa, who seems to be the only one who understands Andy and his strange ability to speak to those who have already died, like his grandma. But once his grandpa passes away rather suddenly, Andy’s abilities grow much faster than before. His grandpa is still there to help Andy with his problems, whether that means getting the girl he loves to notice him or battling evil spirits.<br /><br />I loved the characters. Andy is a compelling narrator who draws readers into his world and into his life. He is brilliant but shy, and he loves math. I really enjoyed all the numbers mentioned throughout the story, as math was one thing Andy could take comfort in. His parents care about him but often misunderstand him, and he has a rocky relationship with his sister. But his grandpa is always there for him, almost literally once he becomes a ghost! Then there’s Andy’s friend Tom, who is intelligent and helps Andy with not only trying to find a way to cure cancer but also finding a way to banish dark spirits. I wish I had that kind of friend! Tom was right at Andy’s side as their friendship grew out of necessity. I even liked Zoe, Andy’s crush. There was a great scene at the end that I hope hinted at something interesting to come in the sequel, which I eagerly look forward to reading.<br /><br />For such a simplistic style, this book is fast-paced and tackles plenty of important issues kids deal with. Making friends, dealing with bullies, trying to get your crush to notice you, making mistakes and resolving personal insecurities, handling the death of a loved one, connecting with your family, all alongside a couple uncommon supernatural issues as well. The black and white drawings at the start of every chapter are cute and a little eerie sometimes, which only added to the book’s compelling atmosphere. There were a few layout issues, like paragraphs and spaces in awkward places, but they were minimal and didn't affect the story in any way.<br /><br />I highly recommend this book to any middle grade kid, especially those who might be reluctant to read. This story will capture their imaginations and inspire their minds and hearts. It will definitely hook them and leave them wanting more. Good thing there’s already a sequel waiting to be enjoyed!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5951712300510606745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_938535063" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/938535063" />
    <a title="Erik This Kid Reviews Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7532583-erik-this-kid-reviews-books"><img alt="Erik This Kid Reviews Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541692975p2/7532583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/938535063?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erik This Kid Reviews Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erik This Kid Reviews Books" href="/user/show/7532583-erik-this-kid-reviews-books">Erik This Kid Reviews Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer938535063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11657583901567727193">Andy is the class nerd. He is picked on and bullied and almost no one will talk to him,(other than to ridicule him). He has only on friend, Tom. Tom is a genius and a fellow nerd. Andy is in love with the prettiest girl in the sixth grade (Zoe), but she will never notice him. Andy keeps his feelings bottled up inside. He is very angry. He wants to talk to his parents, but is afraid to do it. The only person Andy can really open up to is his Grandfather. He can tell his Grandpa anything, but Gran</span>
  <span id="freeText11657583901567727193" style="display:none">Andy is the class nerd. He is picked on and bullied and almost no one will talk to him,(other than to ridicule him). He has only on friend, Tom. Tom is a genius and a fellow nerd. Andy is in love with the prettiest girl in the sixth grade (Zoe), but she will never notice him. Andy keeps his feelings bottled up inside. He is very angry. He wants to talk to his parents, but is afraid to do it. The only person Andy can really open up to is his Grandfather. He can tell his Grandpa anything, but Grandpa has cancer and is going to die. Andy is even more alone. Grandpa tells Andy he is ready to die, that it is his time. He also tells Andy that he will never leave him until he gets Zoe to be his girlfriend. Grandpa is true to his word, even in death. Andy realizes he can still see Grandpa even though he is a ghost. But it’s not just Grandpa, Andy can see all kinds of ghosts walking the Earth! Soon Andy realizes that Zoe is in horrible trouble . He enlists the help of Tom and together they set off to save the day.<br /><br />What I thought- At first I really didn’t like Andy’s character. He was creepy and it sounded like he wanted to hurt people. I really couldn’t relate to him – at first. As I read further, I could understand why Andy was feeling the way he was. He was completely tortured at school and he had no one to talk to. I found myself turning from not liking Andy to rooting for him. Andy just wanted to be himself and have people accept him. The whole part of the plot where Andy develops a super power – to see ghosts – is a cool twist to the plot. Mr. Gadot’s writing style, how the book is narrated, reminded me of Neil Gaiman’s. I like that the story deals with some very tough subjects, (bullying, death of a loved one), but Andy handles them very well and he is a very believable character. The other characters in the book are good, even the minor ones. I like how Andy’s character develops in the story. The trouble that Andy finds Zoe in was an unexpected but very cool twist in the story (not telling you what it is ;) ). I found myself enjoying this story very much.<br />*NOTE I got a free copy of this book in exchange for an honest review</span>

<div id="review_839009629" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/839009629" />
    <a title="Kathy Cunningham" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7643553-kathy-cunningham"><img alt="Kathy Cunningham" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442631752p2/7643553.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/839009629?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Cunningham" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Cunningham" href="/user/show/7643553-kathy-cunningham">Kathy Cunningham</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7643553-kathy-cunningham?shelf=self-published-best-bets">self-published-best-bets</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer839009629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15013631901836861124">Eran Gadot’s SUPERNATURAL HERO is the story of 6th grader Andy and his struggle to fit in. Andy sees himself as a nerd whose only real skills are in math. He has one school friend (fellow math junkie Tom), and he’s often the butt of the other kids’ cruel jokes (they call him “ET” and laugh at him mercilessly). His parents are busy and aloof, paying more attention to his older sister than they ever do to him. His only real support is his Grandpa, who is the only one who really understands him. An</span>
  <span id="freeText15013631901836861124" style="display:none">Eran Gadot’s SUPERNATURAL HERO is the story of 6th grader Andy and his struggle to fit in. Andy sees himself as a nerd whose only real skills are in math. He has one school friend (fellow math junkie Tom), and he’s often the butt of the other kids’ cruel jokes (they call him “ET” and laugh at him mercilessly). His parents are busy and aloof, paying more attention to his older sister than they ever do to him. His only real support is his Grandpa, who is the only one who really understands him. Andy is madly in love with beautiful Zoe, who he calls the “Queen of the School,” but he’s certain she’ll never go out with him, especially because he’s too scared to even talk to her. When his beloved Grandpa dies from cancer, Andy is sure his life is over, too. But then something miraculous happens – Grandpa returns as a ghost to help Andy discover his true potential and win over Zoe and his entire 6th grade class.<br /><br />The best part of this book is Andy, who is totally believable as a lovable loser. He dreams of being one of the “cool kids,” of being invited to birthday parties, and of riding with Zoe on the back of his bike. But he never really believes any of that is possible . . . at least until his Grandpa starts “haunting” him. Andy’s relationship with this man is a beautiful one; Grandpa helps build Andy’s self-esteem and gives him the courage to believe he can be more than a math nerd and class geek. So many kids his age have trouble adjusting to the social life of junior high, and this book can be a real blessing. Andy succeeds because he learns to believe in himself, and that’s a message any young reader can embrace.<br /><br />The weakest part of the book is actually the oddly dark spin it takes in the final section. I loved the relationship between Andy and his Grandpa, and I totally bought into their ghostly meetings (which reminded me a lot of the film “The Sixth Sense”). But when Andy starts seeing demons, it lost me. The final act of the story involves a threat to Zoe and her family, which enables Andy to become a “supernatural hero” and save the day. It was a cute ending, and it’s nice to see Andy recognized as a hero, but it didn’t ring true for me.<br /><br />Additionally, Andy’s crush on Zoe (which seems totally based on how attractive she is, since we don’t get to know her much beyond that) causes him to be less than gracious to another girl in his class. Sally clearly likes Andy, but she’s a nerd, just like he is. And when he tells his Grandpa that going to the movies with Sally would be social suicide, I really wanted something to happen that would show him how wrong that attitude is. His negative view of Sally (because she’s not “cool”) is no different from the negative way Andy has been treated by the “cool kids” in his class. He wants to be a hero so he can win the approval of the popular crowd – and the attention of the “Queen of the School” – but I felt for Sally. She and Andy are very much alike, but he never seems to get that.<br /><br />In spite of those criticisms, this is a book that young readers are sure to enjoy. Andy is an identifiable character who will resonate with any kids who have ever navigated the mine-field of junior high. Gadot’s prose is clear and easy to read, but he never talks down to his readers. And even though this is definitely a “message novel” (i.e. “believe in yourself” and “never give up on your dreams”), it’s never preachy or didactic. I recommend it highly. <br /><br />[Please note: I was provided a copy of this novel for review; the opinions expressed here are my own.]<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15013631901836861124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Harmony David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Harmony David" href="/user/show/39446943-harmony-david">Harmony David</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15930356294580264724">i really follow Andy, who loves his grandfather more than anyone in the entire world while he deals with all the problems a nerdy kids has to on a day to day basis, along with some that are more unusual like a demon that wants to burn down the house of Zoe, the girl that he loves but just can't quite figure out how to talk to. With the help of with grandfather and his best friend Tom (who is incredibly smart) he finds ways to overcome his problems and hopefully eventually get invited to a birthd</span>
  <span id="freeText15930356294580264724" style="display:none">i really follow Andy, who loves his grandfather more than anyone in the entire world while he deals with all the problems a nerdy kids has to on a day to day basis, along with some that are more unusual like a demon that wants to burn down the house of Zoe, the girl that he loves but just can't quite figure out how to talk to. With the help of with grandfather and his best friend Tom (who is incredibly smart) he finds ways to overcome his problems and hopefully eventually get invited to a birthday party.<br />The story opens with Andy, a sixth grader, explaining how he’s the class nerd and nobody in his class likes him. The story soon sets up a basic cliché: Nerd Kid is in love with the Class Princess, is practically ignored by his family, but loves his grandfather very much. At first I was a little uncertain, afraid it would just be some cheesy story.<br /><br />I'm glad I kept reading, though, because the entire story was full of surprises. There were various twists and turns in the story that kept me turning the pages with loads of anticipation.<br /><br />The characters were all interesting in their own way. Andy, of course, was the child everyone can relate to. The feelings of being underappreciated and misunderstood and neglected, these are feelings that many children experience. The same goes for determination and love and bravery and the nervousness that comes from facing school crushes. Andy experiences all of these and more, and the entire story is told in a brilliant way that carries the spirit and imagination—and, most importantly, the voice—of children.<br />he book is well-written, and the illustrations are outstanding. Andy's character is well-developed, and you find yourself rooting for him to become the true Supernatural Hero he wants to be.Recommended</span>

<div id="review_992408616" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/992408616" />
    <a title="Kelsea  David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6041647-kelsea-david"><img alt="Kelsea  David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345004501p2/6041647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/992408616?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelsea  David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelsea  David" href="/user/show/6041647-kelsea-david">Kelsea  David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer992408616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15090833416926868225"> I really wish that this book had been longer. It was a cute read. The beginning was a little hard for me, because poor Andy seems to have been dealt a bad family. I just wanted to cuddle him and tell him everything would be ok. And I loved that he was so close with his grandpa, just like me, so it was something that I could really relate to.<br/><br/>Now let's get into the nitty gritty. The ghosts. So, Andy has been seeing and talking to his grandma's ghost for years, but he suddenly can't understand it </span>
  <span id="freeText15090833416926868225" style="display:none"> I really wish that this book had been longer. It was a cute read. The beginning was a little hard for me, because poor Andy seems to have been dealt a bad family. I just wanted to cuddle him and tell him everything would be ok. And I loved that he was so close with his grandpa, just like me, so it was something that I could really relate to.<br /><br />Now let's get into the nitty gritty. The ghosts. So, Andy has been seeing and talking to his grandma's ghost for years, but he suddenly can't understand it when he see's his grandpa's ghost. That was something I had a hard time with, especially since later in the book you find out he sees all kinds of ghosts. You think he would be more understanding of it all. But really that was the only flaw that I saw in the book.<br /><br />It really felt like a good coming of age story, where Andy realizes that he needs to speak up and be himself and things will go his way. I also really liked a lot of the philosophies that his grandfather taught him. There are quite a few lessons to learn in this book, whether you are a child or an adult. There were also some parts where I got to relive the frustrations of being a child and having no control. Andy couldn’t control anything, his parents didn’t understand him and sent him to therapy, and when his sister bullied him his parents never took his side. I had forgotten that feeling, the one that feels like you have no say over your own life. I thought that came across very strongly here.<br /><br />Definitely a cute read. I give it 4 out of 5 stars, because of the ghost inconsistencies, but other than that it was good. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15090833416926868225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1049697342" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1049697342" />
    <a title="J.p. Ruiz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33092282-j-p-ruiz"><img alt="J.p. Ruiz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405456581p2/33092282.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1049697342?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.p. Ruiz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.p. Ruiz" href="/user/show/33092282-j-p-ruiz">J.p. Ruiz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1049697342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3429630443208988165">Supernatural Hero<br/>By: Eran Gadot<br/>159 pages (Reviewed on 09/08/2014).<br/><br/>In his book, Supernatural Hero, Gadot provides the unique opportunity to peer into young Andy’s life. Gadot beautifully illustrates the real life struggles of a young boy in a world where the “cool” kids ridicule and take sport in harassing the quiet, smart, unpopular child. Andy has a big heart and all he wants to do is share it with the love of his life, Zoe.<br/><br/>Everyone can relate to the uphill social and emotional battle that Andy</span>
  <span id="freeText3429630443208988165" style="display:none">Supernatural Hero<br />By: Eran Gadot<br />159 pages (Reviewed on 09/08/2014).<br /><br />In his book, Supernatural Hero, Gadot provides the unique opportunity to peer into young Andy’s life. Gadot beautifully illustrates the real life struggles of a young boy in a world where the “cool” kids ridicule and take sport in harassing the quiet, smart, unpopular child. Andy has a big heart and all he wants to do is share it with the love of his life, Zoe.<br /><br />Everyone can relate to the uphill social and emotional battle that Andy faces day-to-day. This book is intelligently written and carefully put together in a way that allows the reader to invest their heart into Andy’s life. It is easy to see and experience how easy it is to pass up someone like Andy as he keeps his troubles to himself in his sad and silent life. <br /><br />Supernatural Hero is a heartwarming tale, realistic and magical. It makes you want to cheer as Andy preservers through tragedy and to discover the magical promise that brings him through. I cheered as he broke through the obstacles and wins the girl’s heart. <br /><br />This book is a “must-read” and impossible to put down. It has been a long time since I have read a book that is so honest and true to life. The story is a tear-jerker that allows the reader to join forces with Andy as he silently exposes his life in his heart. The story builds to a climax as we witness the victim (Andy) become the victor in this magical adventure. <br /><br />This story is well written and I look forward to read more of Gadot’s work, he is truly a wonderful story teller. I recommend this book to everyone; do not pass this one up. <br /><br />Blessings,<br />J.P. Ruiz<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3429630443208988165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1061740876" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1061740876" />
    <a title="M. Fonthaunt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35247327-m-fonthaunt"><img alt="M. Fonthaunt" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1061740876?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="M. Fonthaunt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="M. Fonthaunt" href="/user/show/35247327-m-fonthaunt">M. Fonthaunt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1061740876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15062663754420576109">This book is really cute and has plenty to offer for young readers. I read it before giving it to my nephew and I probably enjoyed it as much as he did. The boy in the story is delightfully ordinary at first glance. Young Andy is a middle-schooler who has all the typical problems of others his age. He is a bit of a geek and has girl trouble! Andy's best friend is probably his grandfather who he adores. He can talk to his grandfather about almost anything like it should be with a best friend. He </span>
  <span id="freeText15062663754420576109" style="display:none">This book is really cute and has plenty to offer for young readers. I read it before giving it to my nephew and I probably enjoyed it as much as he did. The boy in the story is delightfully ordinary at first glance. Young Andy is a middle-schooler who has all the typical problems of others his age. He is a bit of a geek and has girl trouble! Andy's best friend is probably his grandfather who he adores. He can talk to his grandfather about almost anything like it should be with a best friend. He also benefits from having his friend Tom at school, who understands being a nerd.<br /><br />Andy also has the other issues kids his age often do. He feels bullied by other kids and siblings. Daily life is often a challenge. I can remember feeling exactly the same way at that age, and sometimes I still do! Things get even stickier for Andy when he goes through a traumatic event (no spoilers here) yet that leads to how he becomes a supernatural hero. Another thing that makes this little book good is that just because he discovers new amazing things - it doesn't solve all his problems overnight. He still has girl trouble!<br /><br />The story has suspense as it goes on and the reader has to find out whether or not Andy finds a way through the trauma, the bullying, and the everyday problems. And, of course, does he win the heart of his true love? The illustrations are also very good and enhance the story. In addition, it is available as an e-book or paperback and I am always on the lookout for books like this since some of the kiddos in my family have e-readers and some prefer print. My nephew wasn't disappointed in this book and I am glad I bought it and read it too.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15062663754420576109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_999901769" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/999901769" />
    <a title="Brielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33167798-brielle"><img alt="Brielle" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/999901769?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brielle" href="/user/show/33167798-brielle">Brielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer999901769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1854855301913268936">Supernatural Hero is a wonderful heartwarming story. I found myself relating to the protagonist Andy, a self-proclaimed class nerd whose parents worry about his social ineptitude and insecurities. I know that I was “that kid” once, and this story would benefit anyone who can relate, and especially kids who cannot yet empathize with Andy. Erin Gadot paints the main character Andy perfectly in a way that will help kids of all ages to understand what it is like to feel like an outsider, a life less</span>
  <span id="freeText1854855301913268936" style="display:none">Supernatural Hero is a wonderful heartwarming story. I found myself relating to the protagonist Andy, a self-proclaimed class nerd whose parents worry about his social ineptitude and insecurities. I know that I was “that kid” once, and this story would benefit anyone who can relate, and especially kids who cannot yet empathize with Andy. Erin Gadot paints the main character Andy perfectly in a way that will help kids of all ages to understand what it is like to feel like an outsider, a life lesson we should all know.<br /><br />The way that Andy deals with his differences is inspiring and captivating, and the powers that he gains are exciting. The illustrations that go along with the story were fun and help the reader connect even more wit this imaginative tale. This coming of age story deals with the complexity of self-esteem, loss, and the true, unharnessed capability of a child that feels powerless and frustrated. Gadot seamlessly weaves this heavy and complicated topics in a child-friendly way, with intriguing supernatural powers that any child would enjoy reading about.<br /><br />Gadot teaches children excellent lessons about family, death, bullying, friendship, and the transformative power of the trials and tribulations that many children face as they grow. Andy's character encourages strength and courage for children as they grow into their differences, or feel misunderstood by their peers and adults. A true page turner from start to finish, I completed this book feeling triumphant and excited for the protagonist and ready for the next installment. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1854855301913268936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_966096349" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/966096349" />
    <a title="Jessica Trotter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6502624-jessica-trotter"><img alt="Jessica Trotter" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/966096349?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Trotter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Trotter" href="/user/show/6502624-jessica-trotter">Jessica Trotter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer966096349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15241932573970847030">Supernatural Hero tells a tale of a middle school aged boy named Andy. Andy is a unique boy who can communicate with ghosts and use to have an imaginary friend. He doesn’t have many friends, feels like he is ignored by his family, never gets invited to birthday parties and is constantly teased at school. He takes comfort though in his smart friend Tom and in his Grandpa. Though all the teasing and torment, he does make time though to fall in love with a girl named Zoe, who he wishes she knew he </span>
  <span id="freeText15241932573970847030" style="display:none">Supernatural Hero tells a tale of a middle school aged boy named Andy. Andy is a unique boy who can communicate with ghosts and use to have an imaginary friend. He doesn’t have many friends, feels like he is ignored by his family, never gets invited to birthday parties and is constantly teased at school. He takes comfort though in his smart friend Tom and in his Grandpa. Though all the teasing and torment, he does make time though to fall in love with a girl named Zoe, who he wishes she knew he was alive. His Grandpa promises him that he will be able to win the heart of Zoe and even though certain circumstances make it a bit harder for him to keep his promise, thus begins Andy’s adventure.<br /><br />This book is a great story for a young reader. Many kids will be able to relate to Andy and enjoy the way his thought process works as well as his tone throughout the book. There are many obstacles that Andy handles quite well for a 6th grader and hopefully children who read this book will learn a bit from him. This story is great and will keep children engaged easily. <br /><br />Each chapter has beautiful illustrations that will help the reader connect even more with the story. The story is well written and while it is a sort of fantasy read, does include realistic life complications. I would definitely recommend to any young adult who is just starting to fall in love with reading. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15241932573970847030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AwJjHulwxlzMyyoHkVBoJyRM98ACX3Y7E5BB5lLyWL370DpS0nAFqwa97QYyA2qSEwidFW1do4gB74VLg4eZlA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+vqIaxHkJxL6yBdNc7Byby0RUZNyVkqADUKVuRnza5gCKNEnKuTk5TC+0EzQ43DaGlU7Rh1UnzMfPVEUyIaqsQ==')})
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_43255392'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43255392-stronghold?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Stronghold: One Man&#39;s Quest to Save the World&#39;s Wild Salmon<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/163538.Tucker_Malarkey?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Tucker Malarkey<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.37 avg rating &mdash; 371 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2019\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer17987769374186801571\">“A powerful and inspiring story. Guido Rahr’s mission to save the wild Pacific salmon leads him into adventures that make for a breathtakingly exciting read.”—Ian Frazier, author of Travels in Siberia\n\nIn the tradition of Mountains Beyond Mountains a<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText17987769374186801571\" style=\"display:none\">“A powerful and inspiring story. Guido Rahr’s mission to save the wild Pacific salmon leads him into adventures that make for a breathtakingly exciting read.”—Ian Frazier, author of Travels in Siberia\n\nIn the tradition of Mountains Beyond Mountains and The Orchid Thief, Stronghold is Tucker Malarkey’s gripping chronicle of an unlikely visionary and his crusade to protect the world’s last bastion for wild salmon. From a young age, Guido Rahr was a misfit among his family and classmates, preferring to spend his time in the natural world. An obsessive fly-fisherman, Rahr noticed when the salmon runs of the Pacific Northwest began to decline—and was one of the few who understood why. As dams, industry, and climate change degraded the homes of these magnificent fish, Rahr saw that the salmon of the Pacific Rim were destined to go the way of their Atlantic brethren: near extinction.\n\nAn improbable and inspiring story, Stronghold takes us on a wild adventure, from Oregon to Alaska to one of the world’s last remaining salmon strongholds in the Russian Far East, a landscape of ecological richness and diversity that is rapidly being developed for oil, gas, minerals, and timber. And along the way Rahr must navigate a tangled web of scientists, conservationists, Russian oligarchs, corrupt officials, impenetrable bureaucracies, and unexpected allies in order to set into motion a plan to secure the survival of the endangered salmon, an extraordinary keystone species whose demise would reverberate across the planet. \n\nTucker Malarkey, who accompanies Rahr to the Russian wilderness and reports on events from up close, has written a clarion call for a sustainable future, a remarkable work of natural history, and a riveting account of a species whose future is closely linked to that of our own.\n\n“All fishermen know that we have to fight to save the waters we love. Stronghold tells a captivating story of the struggle to save the last great salmon rivers.”—Johnny Morris, founder/owner of Bass Pro shops, owner of Cabela’s<\/span>\n  <a
